<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> Used it for about 6 months and loved it, no complaints.  Then it just stopped working.</li>
    <li> So far, so good. While I read that some people had problems with this hair dryer, I had purchased it before, and that one lasted 4 1/2 years. Considering the price, and the fact that I returned one (to a drug store, not to Amazon) that cost more than twice the price and didn&#x27;t work nearly as well, I decided to take my chances. It dries hair quickly without breakage. I did notice that now on the info they include, it tells you not to wrap the cord around the handle for storage. I always did that, although I never pulled it tight to where it broke the wires or covering on them, so maybe that contributed to the problem people have had? Seems to be well made. I will update this review if it breaks quickly.</li>
    <li> Don&#x27;t buy! After using it for a little over 6 months mine suddenly caught on fire.&lt;br /&gt;It stopped working, sparkles came out of the handle, the electric cord caught on fire. I was able to unplug it.&lt;br /&gt;The sparkles damaged my wall bathroom mirror. But at least I didn&#x27;t die from electrocution!</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve used this dryer several times, and it is faster and quieter than my previous (deceased) hair dryer. My hair gets dryer faster, plus the Revlon dryer is very light, making it so easy to use without straining my arms for so long. I haven&#x27;t used attachments on a blow dryer in so long, I almost forgot what a convenience they are. In truth, I tossed out my old dryer&#x27;s attachments because they kept popping off while the dryer was working. No such problem here -- the attachments seem to snap securely into place and stay there until they are removed! Excellent price for a dryer that performs this well. I may ultimately purchase a second one for the guest bathroom.</li>
    <li> I liked this Revlon hair dryer as it dried my hair quickly and was relatively lightweight.  I&#x27;m on my third one though within a year.  It only takes my hair 5 minutes to blow dry, once daily.  This hair dryer should last much longer.  I&#x27;m on my search for another dryer.</li>
    <li> This hair dryer is great and cheap. I don&#x27;t use one all the time but when I do I expect it to make my hair dry and not hot. This dryer does not damage my hair and it&#x27;s still in great shape. My only concern is it smells pretty bad like something is burnt when I turn it on but it doesn&#x27;t bother me because I understand it has to heat up.</li>
    <li> It is not terrible but I would not buy it again.  It seems like over time ( and not a long time) the dryer has lost some of its air power.  I thought it used to actually move my hair while I was drying it now it does not.  It blows two temperatures of hot air and the cold shot still works, I have cleaned the filters out but it just takes forever to dry my med length hair.  I want a blow dryer that BLOWS the hair.  This one does not.  The other issue I have is with the design.  The toggle switch power is right where you hold the dryer so I am CONSTANTLY turning it off accidentally while drying.</li>
    <li> I have been using the hairdryer for a while and everything had been working fine. Yesterday however, after blow drying for about 5 minutes, I noticed it started to lose power. I thought I simply had to clean the filter, but before I managed to reach up and turn it off there were sparks and smoke coming out from both the outlet and blow dryer itself. As this was right where I held my hand, I dropped it in panic and unplugged it immediately. In the split second that the dryer ignited, the palm of my hand had turned black from the smoke. Most of this washed away, but I was left with a painful burn that has yet to go away. Upon closer inspection I noticed that the cable had broken where it connects to the dryer, and reading other reviews this seems to be a common problem. I have never bent the wire at this point, as I consistently hang it using the attached hook. This must simply be bad engineering, and seeing how this could be dangerous (even potentially lethal), I cannot recommend this hair dryer to anyone else.</li>

    <li> As an electrician I am somewhat qualified to review why this hairdryer fails and is a danger. My hairdryer failed to last a year because the cord just under the strain relief has severed internally under the rubber from mechanical fatigue. When this happens the dryer will lose power and regain power if you flex the cord, eventually if you keep using it, the arcing at the break will overheat and the cord will: smoke, burn, pop, expose the conductors and maybe catch on fire. All they need to do is use a higher quality cord, otherwise this dryer would be fine. As it is, it&#x27;s a hazard that is not worth it.</li>

This Revlon is amazing, though--my hair is so straight, sleek, and shiny, without having to apply a bunch of creams or shining sprays. It saves a lot of time! It comes with two attachments (diffuser, concentrator)--I&#x27;ve only used the concentrator to straighten my hair and it takes around six minutes and works effectively.    Also, a HUGE bonus is its lightweight! The comparable Conair version (nearly same price, ionic) is so so much heavier, while this hairdryer is easy to move, so I can pick it up and use it all over my hair.  The only con about this as others have mentioned is that you have to hold it carefully or else your fingers will accidentally turn the hairdryer off--the buttons move easily and are near where you place your fingers to hold it.    Bottom Line: This is the best hairdryer for the price. When I used other hairdryers, my hair is very noticeably frizzier and less shiny compared to this Revlon.     <li> I bought my first RV544 after a \\&quot;blow-dry 101\\&quot; class with my stylist. Noted features: 1) ionic, 2) tourmaline, 3) concentrator attachment that has a narrow opening. DO NOT get rid of your concentrator attachment when you buy a new blow dryer! I have very straight, flat hair so a diffuser is useless for me, but the concentrator is essential. It builds body and volume.  Some dryers have a funneling \\&quot;concentrator\\&quot; that is so fat it could hardly be concentrating anything. Look for a slim opening. This dryer has it.    Another favorite feature: it&#x27;s VERY lightweight. I style my hair from start to finish with my blow dryer, no curling/straightening tools, just the dryer and 2 brushes. Technique is important. I have a great stylist who taught me this. Anyway the light weight is great both for use and for travel.     And, the attachments snap on and pivot easily in a groove on the end of the blower. This is important because a dryer that has a concentrator that just fits over the end but doesn&#x27;t snap in place will make you FURIOUS. I am talking about the concentrator either blowing off mid-process, or being so tight that you can&#x27;t get it off nor can you pivot it. I have carpal tunnel syndrome and it is very painful to try to adjust the concentrator. This one is so very easy.    I have owned 2 of these dryers and I&#x27;m ready to purchase my 3rd. One of my daughters took over #1, someone burned a hole in the concentrator of #2, and to replace it I bought an expensive salon dryer thinking price meant value. That&#x27;s the one that has been driving me nuts. I&#x27;m going to retire the pricey dryer to the \\&quot;emergency\\&quot; drawer and buy this one again.     If you have read this review and are interested in technique, check out this link:   [...]</li>

    <li> Ok, that&#x27;s not true. Ions are completely, 100% real. But the real question is whether or not they have magical powers to make your hair soft, silky, and extra shiny. Well, here&#x27;s the answer: It&#x27;s all marketing BS. Seriously, what kind of ions are they? Are they positively charged or negatively charged? The lack of detail offered does not inspire confidence.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But aside from the ions, this device effectively expels hot air. When I turn it on and point it at my hair when it is wet, my hair dries. When I use the air focusing attachment in conjunction with a round brush, my hair is straightened. When I use the diffuser it&#x27;s not straight. But it&#x27;s also not pretty. I&#x27;m pretty sure I&#x27;m using it wrong or something.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In all seriousness however, this hair dryer is perfectly effective. Don&#x27;t waste your money on a more expensive hair dryer unless it comes with robotic arms which style your hair for you. This is a heating element and a fan, an incredibly simple device.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Initially when I began my quest for a new hair dryer I was overwhelmed by all the choices, and I began doing research on what makes a hair dryer good. I even made a spreadsheet! I began googling and was told that there are multiple factors which are important: Ions, ceramic heating element, type of motor, and wattage.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Ions: I&#x27;ve already discussed these in the beginning of the post. But for further clarification, I&#x27;ll include information from a more reputable source than someone who calls herself \\&quot;CatMonkey\\&quot;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; \\&quot;How do \\&quot;ionic\\&quot; hair dryers affect the hair, short-term and long term?&lt;br /&gt;  In the short term, the ions produced by an ionic hair dryer help reduce static electricity. Ordinary blow dryers tend to produce  static electricity. Having extra charged particles (ions) in the air allows any built-up electrical charge (static electricity) to be transferred through the air to other nearby surfaces. This doesn&#x27;t have much effect, since the \\&quot;frizzy\\&quot; effects of static electricity fade within a few minutes anyway. Coating the hair with gel or some kind of conductive conditioner would have a much stronger and lasting effect than ions, which only exist while the hair dryer is running. In the long term, ions are more reactive than other molecules, so they probably cause the hair and/or natural oils to be oxidized and the hair to become more brittle. But this is probably a smaller effect than the use of conditioners (good) or hot air (bad). More worrisome is that ionic generators generate ozone, which is good high in the atmosphere but bad here at ground level. Ozone contributes to smog and can cause lung irritation.\\&quot; Source: University of California Santa Barbara: Science Line ([...]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, long story short: Ions might have some effect, but it&#x27;s negligible compared to a good conditioner, and ionic generators generate ozone. I couldn&#x27;t find a hair dryer without \\&quot;ionic technology\\&quot; but skip the ones with an ionic generator and buy a fancy conditioner instead.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Ceramic heating element: I had a hard time finding a hair dryer that wasn&#x27;t ceramic. Whether or not this makes it better or worse is unknown to me. Supposedly it helps the hair dryer heat more evenly. I&#x27;m calling BS on this too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. Type of motor: Supposedly the type of motor makes a difference, whether it&#x27;s AC or DC. For this I asked an electrical engineer if this could possibly make a difference. He was very confused as to why I was asking him such a dumb question because there would be zero impact on it. \\&quot;FFS CatMonkey, it&#x27;s a heating element and a fan. It&#x27;s not complicated. Why are you wasting so much time on this? Don&#x27;t you have an organic chemistry midterm tomorrow? The type of current doesn&#x27;t matter at all.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. Wattage: Some websites said that higher wattage meant higher heat, others said that it wasn&#x27;t a valid indicator of heat output as there was significant variation between high wattage dryers and heat output.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now we&#x27;ve come to the end, I evaluated those four factors and eventually realized that there are really only a few criteria which are important to me. Cord length, included attachments, and weight. This dryer has a nice long cord, two attachments, and it&#x27;s not super heavy. Oh, and it&#x27;s less than $20. Perfect!w we&#x27;ve come to the end, I evaluated those four factors and eventually realized that there are really only a few criteria which are important to me. Cord length, included attachments, and weight. This dryer has a nice long cord, two attachments, and it&#x27;s not super heavy. Oh, and it&#x27;s less than $20. Perfect!</li>

    <li> I have naturally curly hair which means... naturally frizzy hair, if anything goes wrong which it usually does. I have used an ionic, ceramic hair dryer for a while now. Never noticed a huge difference with that. The improvement from this model is the diffuser. I haven&#x27;t used other diffusers, so I have no basis of comparison but if you are a curly girl or guy, adding a diffuser to your arsenal is worth it. It&#x27;s a different way of drying your hair. I&#x27;m still adjusting to it-- you place the end of the diffuser against your head in one area and hold it there while it gently puffs air all around it. We&#x27;re supposed to tousle our hair with the diffuser &amp;#34;fingers&amp;#34; but I mostly bonk myself in the head when I do that-- much better to use the &amp;#34;fingers&amp;#34; to gently cup the end of your hair so it gets scrunched up against your head-- and then hold it there for a minute. Then move on to a new spot on your head. What I&#x27;ve noticed is that my hair curls more evenly than before. I used to have areas that would flatten a bit even with the low speed of a regular blow dryer. You can imagine how lovely that looked. Now all the areas are a bit more uniformly curled and there are fewer flyaways on top. Other blow dryers with diffuser attachments may do the same thing-- this one was a good price and had the ionic/ceramic combo I wanted. I&#x27;m very happy with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One note-- the diffuser is pretty big so you&#x27;ll need a deeper drawer or a bit more cupboard space to store it.</li>

I contacted HoT to inquire about which model of comb would fit this dryer, since most comb attachments are expensive and I did not want to waste my money. They were very fast to respond but no one could tell me if there was one available that would fit. After a week, I received an email saying that they do not make a comb attachment that would fit this particular model. They said that this particular dryer has a specific nozzle so no other attachments from them, or other brands would fit it. I was disappointed, since nowhere in the package or description page does it say this. Perhaps I was naive to think that a company would never think not to make other attachments that would fit their best selling economy model, other than the standard out of the box ones. I was hesitant at first because the price is low, but it really does the job of a more expensive product.  I am buying another one so when this one finally bites the dust I have another.</li>
